# Excalidraw Data

## Text Elements
I would say one of the best resources on the topic would be 
Orientation, Rotation, Velocity and Acceleration, and the SRM 
https://www.sedris.org/wg8home/Documents/WG80485.pdf ^auk9WL23

from what I remember, we use a left handed system where the roll and pitch are the same but the yaw is about
a z-axis facing "upwards". ^vYAJRS2z

https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euler_angles
This is another good resource on the topic and it very nicely gives us a table 

 ^ws0nh2jQ

The only caveat being that this does not warn us of gimbal locking cases.  ^nRvAQlNA

works really well. ^RrTLKwhv

such cases are difficult to handle.



Fortunately, for small rotations, I hope that since rotations are SO(3) groups, there will be no big issues. ^LHQHhC0v

More granularity does improve the jaggedness of the path. But lets see if we can do any better:  ^IeU3G2uA

From what I can tell, getting to know more about the movement constraints can help us model more
effectively, being able to control different angles at the same time

A ligament like movement mechanism can also open up pathways to move along axes other that those
of the gimbal. ^QiIMuKhF

## Element Links
auk9WL23: https://www.sedris.org/wg8home/Documents/WG80485.pdf
